  The decorated function will map any positional arguments after the ``*`` to\n   105→    the corresponding keyword arguments and issue a deprecation warning.\n   106→\n   107→    The decorator takes If these are missing, augment the ordering with a descendant\n   427→        primary key.\n   428→        \"\"\"\n   429→        ordering = list(ordering)\n   430→        ordering_fields = set()\n   431→        total_ordering_fields = {\"pk\"} | {\n   432→            field.attname\n   433→            for field in self.lookup_opts.fields\n   434→            if field.unique and not field.null\n   435→        }\n   436→        for part in ordering:\n   437→            # Search for single field providing a total ordering.\n   438→            field_name = None\n   439→            if isinstance(part, str):\n   440→                field_name = part.lstrip(\"-\")\n   441→            elif isinstance(part, F):\n   442→                field_name = part.name\n   443→            elif isinstance(part, OrderBy) and isinstance(part.expression, F):\n   444→                field_name = part.expression.name\n   445→            if field_name:\n   446→                # Normalize attname references by using get_field().\n   447→                try:\n   448→                    field = self.lookup_opts.get_field(field_name)\n   449→                except FieldDoesNotExist:\n   450→                    # Could be \"?\" for random ordering or a related field\n   451→                    # lookup. Skip this part of introspection for now.\n   455→                if field.remote_field and field_name == field.name:\n   456→                    continue\n   457→                if field.attname in total_ordering_fields:\n   458→                    break\n   459→                ordering_fields.add(field.attname)\n   460→        else:\n   461→            # Then, any manually-specified ordering\n        from the query string overrides anything. Finally, a deterministic\n        order is guaranteed by calling _get_deterministic_ordering() with the\n        constructed ordering.\n        \"\"\"\n        params = self.params\n        ordering = list(\n            self.model_admin.get_ordering(request) or self._get_default_ordering()\n        )\n        if params.get(ORDER_VAR):\n            # Search for a\n        single field or unique together set of fields providing a total\n        ordering. If these are missing, augment the ordering with a descendant\n        primary key.\n        \"\"\"\n        ordering = list(ordering)\n        ordering_fields = set()\n        total_ordering_fields = {\"pk\"} | {\n            field.attname\n            for field in self.lookup_opts.fields\n            if field.unique and not field.null\n        }\n        for part in ordering:\n            # Search for single field providing a total ordering.\n            field_name = None\n            if isinstance(part, str):\n                field_name = part.lstrip(\"-\")\n            elif isinstance(part, F):\n                field_name = part.name\n            elif isinstance(part, OrderBy) and isinstance(part.expression, F):\n                field_name = part.expression.name\n            if field_name:\n                # Normalize attname references by using get_field().\n                try:\n                    field = self.lookup_opts.get_field(field_name)\n                except FieldDoesNotExist:\n                    # Could be \"?\" for random ordering or a related field\n                    # lookup. Skip this part of introspection for now.\n                    continue\n                # Ordering by a related field name orders by the referenced\n                # model's ordering. Skip this part of introspection for now.\n                if field.remote_field and field_name == field.name:\n                    continue\n                if field.attname in total_ordering_fields:\n                    break\n                ordering_fields.add(field.attname)\n        else:\n            # We must cope with more than one column having the same underlying\n        # sort field, so we base things on column numbers.\n        ordering = self._get_default_ordering()\n        ordering_fields = {}\n        if ORDER_VAR not in self.params:\n            # for ordering specified on ModelAdmin or model Meta, we don't know\n            # the right column numbers absolutely, because there might be more\n            # than one column associated with that ordering, so we guess.\n            for field in ordering:\n                if isinstance(field, (Combinable, OrderBy)):\n                    if not isinstance(field, OrderBy):\n                        field = field.asc()\n                    if isinstance(field.expression, F):\n                        order_type = \"desc\" if field.descending else \"asc\"\n                        field = field.expression.name\n                    else:\n                        continue\n                elif field.startswith(\"-\"):\n                    field = field.removeprefix(\"-\")\n                    order_type = \"desc\"\n                else:\n                    order_type = \"asc\"\n                for index, attr in enumerate(self.list_display):\n                    if self.get_ordering_field(attr) == field:\n                        ordering_fields[index] = order_type\n                        break\n        else:\n            for p in self.params[ORDER_VAR].split(\".\"):\n                none, pfx, idx = p.rpartition(\"-\")\n                try:\n                    idx = int(idx)\n                except ValueError:\n                    continue  # skip it\n                ordering_fields[idx] = \"desc\" if pfx == \"-\" else \"asc\"\n        return ordering_fields\n\n    def get_queryset(self, request, exclude_parameters=None):\n        # First, we collect all the declared list filters.\n        (\n            self.filter_specs,\n            self.has_filters,\n            remaining_lookup_params,\n            filters_may_have_duplicates,\n            self.has_active_filters,\n        ) = self.get_filters(request)\n        # Then, we let every list filter modify the queryset to its liking.\n        qs = self.root_queryset\n        for filter_spec in self.filter_specs:\n            if (\n                exclude_parameters is None\n                or filter_spec.expected_parameters() != exclude_parameters\n            ):\n                new_qs = filter_spec.queryset(request, qs)\n                if new_qs is not None:\n                    qs = new_qs\n\n        try:\n            # Finally, we apply the remaining lookup parameters from the query\n            # string (i.e. those that haven't already been processed by the\n            # filters).\n            q_object = build_q_object_from_lookup_parameters(remaining_lookup_params)\n            qs = qs.filter(q_object)\n        except (SuspiciousOperation, ImproperlyConfigured):\n            # Allow certain types of errors to be re-raised as-is so that the\n            # caller can treat them in a special way.\n            raise\n        except Exception as e:\n            # Every other error is caught with a naked except, because we don't\n            # have any other way of validating lookup parameters. They might be\n            # invalid if the keyword arguments are incorrect, or if the values\n            # are not in the correct type, so we might get FieldError,\n            # ValueError, ValidationError, or ?.\n            raise IncorrectLookupParameters(e)\n\n        if not qs.query.select_related:\n            qs = self.apply_select_related(qs)\n\n        # Set ordering.\n        ordering = self.get_ordering(request, qs)\n        qs = qs.order_by(*ordering)\n\n        # Apply search results\n        qs, search_may_have_duplicates = self.model_admin.get_search_results(\n            request,\n            qs,\n            self.query,\n        )\n\n        # Set query string for clearing all filters.\n        self.clear_all_filters_qs = self.get_query_string(\n            new_params=remaining_lookup_params,\n            remove=self.get_filters_params(),\n        )\n        # Remove duplicates from results, if necessary\n        if filters_may_have_duplicates | search_may_have_duplicates:\n            return qs.distinct()\n        else:\n            return qs\n\n    def apply_select_related(self, qs):\n        if self.list_select_related is True:\n            return qs.select_related()\n\n        if self.list_select_related is False:\n            if self.has_related_field_in_list_display():\n                return qs.select_related()\n\n        if self.list_select_related:\n            return qs.select_related(*self.list_select_related)\n        return qs\n\n    def has_related_field_in_list_display(self):\n        for field_name in self.list_display:\n            try:\n                field = self.lookup_opts.get_field(field_name)\n            except FieldDoesNotExist:\n                pass\n            else:\n                if isinstance(field.remote_field, ManyToOneRel):\n                    # <FK>_id field names don't require a join.\n                    if field_name != field.attname:\n                        return True\n        return False\n\n    def url_for_result(self, result):\n        pk = getattr(result, self.pk_attname)\n        return reverse(\n            \"admin:%s_%s_change\" % (self.opts.app_label, self.opts.model_name),\n            args=(quote(pk),),\n            current_app=self.model_admin.admin_site.name,\n        )\n","numLines":622,"startLine":1,"totalLines":622}}}

Looking back at the bug report and the code:\n\nThe issue is that when a ForeignKey field is configured for filtering (via list_filter), but the related model has no rows in the database, the filter still appears in the sidebar but only shows \"All\" option. This is confusing for users.\n\nLooking at the code:\n1. `RelatedFieldListFilter` (extends `FieldListFilter`) - used for ForeignKey fields\n   - It overrides `has_output()` to check `len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1`\n   - Where `extra` is 1 if the field is nullable or many-to-many, else 0\n   - So if there are 0 choices and extra is 0, it returns False (good!)\n   - But if extra is 1, it returns True even with 0 choices (bad!)\n\n2. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_011ytVVV8gmaC1jCF44Gnzco","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"The Python 3.11 issue is blocking me. Let me just work with the code analysis instead. Based on my reading of the code, I believe the issue is:The `FieldListFilter.has_output()` method returns `True` unconditionally. This means filters that inherit from it without overriding `has_output()` will always show, even if they have no meaningful choices.The filters that DON'T override has_output() are:- `BooleanFieldListFilter`\n- `ChoicesFieldListFilter`\n- `DateFieldListFilter`\n- `AllValuesFieldListFilter`\n- `EmptyFieldListFilter`\n\nThe filters that DO override has_output() are:\n- `SimpleListFilter` - checks `len(self.lookup_choices) > 0`\n- `RelatedFieldListFilter` - checks `len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1`\n\nNow, the bug report mentions specifically ForeignKey relationships. Let me think about this more carefully:When a ForeignKey field is in list_filter:- If there are no related objects in the database, `RelatedFieldListFilter.lookup_choices` will be empty\n- The `has_output()` method will check if `len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1`\n- If the field is NOT nullable (extra=0): returns `0 + 0 > 1` = False (correct!)  \n- If the field IS nullable (extra=1): returns `0 + 1 > 1` = False (correct!)\n\nSo actually RelatedFieldListFilter seems correct. But wait, let me check the condition again. It says `> 1`, which means it needs at least 2 choices. But for a simple filter with just \"All\" and one other option, that would be 2 choices:- \"All\" is always shown (from choices() method)\n- Plus one other choice from lookup_choicesActually, looking at the code, \"All\" is not part of `lookup_choices`. It's yielded separately in the `choices()` method. So `lookup_choices` only contains the actual filter options.\n\n\nIf `lookup_choices` is empty, there are no actual filter options beyond \"All\". The `> 1` check ensures at least one real choice exists alongside \"All\". When this condition fails, the filter correctly hides. But I'm wondering if the real problem surfaces elsewhere—perhaps when a ForeignKey should populate choices but doesn't, or with a different field type entirely. Let me look at the bug report again to see what specifically triggers the issue.\n\nThe core complaint is that the filter widget appears even when zero related objects exist in the database. This points to `has_output()` returning True when it should return False. Tracing the logic: `views/main.py` line 221 checks `if spec and spec.has_output():` before adding the filter. For a RelatedFieldListFilter with no related objects, `has_output()` should return False and prevent the filter from appearing. So either `has_output()` is broken, or the choices aren't being computed correctly in the first place. I need to examine how `lookup_choices` gets populated in `RelatedFieldListFilter.__init__` to understand where the disconnect happens. meaningful choices means the filter has no distinct values to display. For RelatedFieldListFilter, that's when no related objects exist. For ChoicesFieldListFilter, it's when all objects share the same choice value. For AllValuesFieldListFilter, it's when there's only one distinct value in the data.\n\nThe solution involves checking if `lookup_choices` is populated in `has_output()` for filters that use it. Some filters like BooleanFieldListFilter, DateFieldListFilter, and EmptyFieldListFilter should always display since they have predefined options. RelatedFieldListFilter and AllValuesFieldListFilter need the empty check since their options depend on the data.\n\nChoicesFieldListFilter is trickier—it relies on `field.flatchoices` rather than `lookup_choices`, so I need to verify whether an empty choices list would cause `has_output()` to return False appropriately. The issue is that filters that inherit from `FieldListFilter` without overriding `has_output()` will always show, even when they have no meaningful choices to display.\n\nLooking at the inheritance hierarchy:\n- `ListFilter` - base class with abstract `has_output()`\n- `FacetsMixin` - mixin for facets support\n- `SimpleListFilter` - overrides has_output() to check `len(self.lookup_choices) > 0` ✓\n- `FieldListFilter` - base class for field-based filters, has_output() returns `True` (always shows)\n  - `RelatedFieldListFilter` - overrides has_output() ✓\n    - `RelatedOnlyFieldListFilter` - inherits from RelatedFieldListFilter ✓\n  - `BooleanFieldListFilter` - doesn't override has_output()\n  - `ChoicesFieldListFilter` - doesn't override has_output()\n  - `DateFieldListFilter` - doesn't override has_output()\n  - `AllValuesFieldListFilter` - doesn't override has_output()\n  - `EmptyFieldListFilter` - doesn't override has_output()\n\nFor most of these, always showing is probably fine:\n- `BooleanFieldListFilter` - shows \"Yes\", \"No\", \"Unknown\" (always has options)\n- `DateFieldListFilter` - shows \"Any date\", \"Today\", \"Past 7 days\", etc. (always has options)\n- `EmptyFieldListFilter` - shows \"All\", \"Empty\", \"Not empty\" (always has options)\n\nBut for these two, we should check if they have meaningful choices:\n\n\n- `ChoicesFieldListFilter` - should check if `field.flatchoices` is non-empty or has non-None values\n- `AllValuesFieldListFilter` - should check if `lookup_choices` is non-empty\n\nFor `ChoicesFieldListFilter`, the filter registration at line 461 checks `bool(f.choices)`, so it's only registered for fields that have choices defined. When the queryset is empty, `lookup_choices` will be empty too, yet the filter still renders with just an \"All\" option. The filter should be hidden entirely if there are no values to display.\n\nThe catch-all filter `AllValuesFieldListFilter` is the problematic one here, though I need to reconsider whether `RelatedFieldListFilter` might be involved since the bug report mentions ForeignKey relationships. Let me check if `RelatedFieldListFilter` has a similar issue with the condition `len(self.lookup_choices` The issue is that `> 1` is too restrictive—it should be `>= 1` to display the filter when there's at least one choice available. However, this creates a problem for nullable fields with no related objects, where only the None option exists. From a UX standpoint, showing a filter with only a None option seems unnecessary, so the logic needs to account for whether we're actually providing meaningful filtering options beyond just the empty value.\n\nThe real fix should be `> 0` instead. This would show the filter when there's at least one related object to choose from, while still hiding it when there are zero objects and the field is non-nullable. For nullable fields with no objects, it would display the None option, which may or may not be desired depending on the use case. The key insight is that a single related object should still display the filter—users need the ability to choose between \"All\" and that specific object. , I'm conflating the operators. `> 0` and `>= 1` are the same thing—both require at least one item. The current code uses `len(lookup_choices) + extra > 1`, which demands at least two items, but it should be `> 0` to show the filter whenever there's at least one meaningful choice available. Testing this logic: with zero non-nullable objects the condition fails (correct), with zero nullable objects it also fails since `0 + 1 > 0` is true but we need to verify the nullable case properly. `0 + 0 > 1` evaluates to False, so the filter shouldn't display. Yet the bug report indicates it does show up when there are zero related objects. This suggests either the condition itself is incorrect, the filter type involved isn't RelatedFieldListFilter, or the values being evaluated aren't what I expect. Let me reconsider whether the logic should actually be checking a different threshold or if there's something else determining visibility. Looking at the choices() method, it always yields \"All\" first, then one choice per item in lookup_choices, plus optionally \"None\" if include_empty_choice is True.
